            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Selenium (Se)-based materials for sodium (ion) batteries are currently attracting extensive attentions owing to their fast kinetics and excellent cyclability; at the same time, achieving high Se content, which is crucial to maintain the competitive edge over other kinds of electrode materials, still remains a challenge.  We developed a confined annealing method which allows us to convert pristine metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) directly into selenium/selenide/carbon composites.  It is a simultaneous process of carbonization, selenization and Se vapor deposition, and the combination of elemental Se and selenide results in a record-high Se content of 76 wt%, enhanced capacity and rate capability (490 and 384 mA h g-1 at 0.1 and 2.0 A g-1) exceeding most documented Se-based materials.  The produced composites also exhibit excellent cycle stability (no decay for 700 cycles at 2 A g-1), which is correlated to dominant capacitive charge transport mode and the MOF-derived robust structure.  Our work not only offers a proof of concept that Se content can be maximized by confining Se through both vapor deposition and chem. bonding with transition metals, but also demonstrates a general and green selenization approach without using any toxic or flammable chems.  The introduced method will probably prevail for its wide applicability on various metal-contg. precursors, and even be expanded to the fabrication of sulfur- and phosphor-based composites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpx7sqXIGeUJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxCd2O4oOa5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisVWmtrk%253D&amp;md5=97699d2ea553023ab4f80c20adc08cff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-016-1394-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Embedding CoS2 nanoparticles in N-doped carbon nanotube hollow frameworks for enhanced lithium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jintao; Yu, Le; Lou, Xiong Wen David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The construction of metal sulfides-carbon nanocomposites with a hollow structure is highly attractive for various energy storage and conversion technologies.  Herein, we report a facile two-step method for prepg. a nanocomposite with CoS2 nanoparticles in N-doped carbon nanotube hollow frameworks (NCNTFs).  Starting from zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) particles, in situ reduced metallic cobalt nanocrystals expedite the formation of the hierarchical hollow frameworks from staggered carbon nanotubes via a carbonization process.  After a follow-up sulfidation reaction with sulfur powder, the embedded cobalt crystals are transformed into CoS2 nanoparticles.  Benefitting from the robust hollow frameworks made of N-doped carbon nanotubes and highly active CoS2 ultrafine nanoparticles, this advanced nanocomposite shows greatly enhanced lithium storage properties when evaluated as an electrode for lithium-ion batteries.  Impressively, the resultant CoS2/NCNTF material delivers a high specific capacity of ∼937 mAh·g-1 at a c.d. of 1.0 A·g-1 with a cycle life longer than 160 cycles.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CoS2 Nanoparticles Wrapping on Flexible Freestanding Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers with High Performance for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Huang, Yajun; Gong, Lunlun; Zhang, Heping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploration for stable and high-powered electrode materials is significant due to the growing demand for energy storage and also challengeable to the development and application of Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Among all promising electrode materials for NIBs, transition-mental sulfides have been identified as potential candidates owing to their distinct physics-chem. characteristics.  In this work, CoS2 nanomaterials anchored into multichannel carbon nanofibers (MCNFs), synthesized via a facile solvothermal method with a sulfidation process, are studied as flexible free-standing electrode materials for NIBs.  CoS2 nanoparticles uniformly distributed in the vertical and horizontal multichannel networks.  Such nanoarchitecture can not only support space for vol. expansion of CoS2 during discharge/charge process, but also facilitate ion/electron transport along the interfaces.  In particular, the CoS2@MCNF electrode delivers an impressively high specific capacity (537.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), extraordinarily long-term cycling stability (315.7 mAh g-1 at at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), and excellent rate capacity (537.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 201.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) for sodium storage.  Free-standing CoS2@MCNF composites with mech. flexibility provide a promising electrode material for high-powered NIBs and flexible cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsuDlBVpRg67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4dLyR5vYcCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFyrurbE&amp;md5=c481fd52012b54cae7f1e150c5213ca4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201403579"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Synthesis of Ultrasmall CoS2 Nanoparticles within Thin N-Doped Porous Carbon Shell for High Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qingfei; Zou, Ruqiang; Xia, Wei; Ma, Jin; Qiu, Bin; Mahmood, Asif; Zhao, Ruo; Yang, Yangyuchen; Xia, Dingguo; Xu, Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cobalt sulfide (CoS2) is considered one of the most promising alternative anode materials for high-performance lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) by virtue of its remarkable elec. cond., high theor. capacity, and low cost.  However, it suffers from a poor cycling stability and low rate capability because of its vol. expansion and dissoln. of the polysulfide intermediates in the org. electrolytes during the battery charge/discharge process.  In this study, a novel porous carbon/CoS2 composite is prepd. by using nano metal-org. framework (MOF) templates for high-performance LIBs.  The as-made ultrasmall CoS2 (15 nm) nanoparticles in N-rich carbon exhibit promising lithium storage properties with negligible loss of capacity at high charge/discharge rate.  At a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, a capacity of 560 mA h g-1 is maintained after 50 cycles.  Even at a c.d. as high as 2500 mA g-1, a reversible capacity of 410 mA h g-1 is obtained.  The excellent and highly stable battery performance should be attributed to the synergism of the ultrasmall CoS2 particles and the thin N-rich porous carbon shells derived from nanosized MOF precursors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3z8NxFPi7-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4dLyR5vYcCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvF2ktbw%253D&amp;md5=a34fdf5e886deae3489334278d710a66</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.09.092"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D spongy CoS2 nanoparticles/carbon composite as high-performance anode material for lithium/sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yaohui; Wang, Nana; Sun, Changhui; Lu, Zhenxiao; Xue, Pan; Tang, Bin; Bai, Zhongchao; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A spongy CoS2/carbon composite assembled from CoS2 nanoparticles (∼20 nm) homogeneously anchored on a spongy carbon matrix was synthesized through a facile freeze-drying method and a hydrothermal process.  As anode material for lithium/sodium ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs), this composite shows significantly enhanced lithium/sodium storage performance with the synergetic effects due to the elec. cond. of the carbon matrix and the porous structure, which provide buffer spaces for vol. expansion during charge/discharge processes and feasible transfer pathways for electrons/ions.  The electrochem. results demonstrate that the spongy CoS2/carbon composite is an outstanding anode material for LIBs and SIBs.  It delivers a high specific capacity of 610 mAh g-1 at 500 mA g-1 after 120 cycles in LIBs and 330 mAh g-1 at 500 mA g-1 after 60 cycles in SIBs, resp.  Moreover, the freeze-drying/hydrothermal process developed in this work could be useful for the construction of many other high-capacity metal sulfide composites as electrode materials for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwXdfLzDrWz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4dLyR5vYcCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFGntr3O&amp;md5=bec339669bfe46b9b745e69b715fe77d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201606776"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Formation of CoS2 Nanobubble Hollow Prisms for Highly Reversible Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Le; Yang, Jing Fan; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have been intensively used as the templates/precursors to synthesize complex hollow structures for various energy-related applications.  Herein a facile two-step diffusion-controlled strategy is reported to generate novel MOFs derived hierarchical hollow prisms composed of Nanosized CoS2 bubble-like subunits.  Uniform zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) hollow prisms assembled by interconnected nanopolyhedra are first synthesized via a transformation process.  Afterwards, these ZIF-67 building blocks are converted into CoS2 bubble-like hollow particles to form the complex hollow prisms through a sulfidation reaction with an addnl. annealing treatment.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly reversible Na ion storage in N-doped polyhedral carbon-coated transition-metal chalcogenides by optimizing the nanostructure and surface engineering</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Gong, Lunlun; Shi, Long; Deng, Yurui; Zhang, Heping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal chalcogenides (TMCs) have been attracting widespread attention due to their high lithium/sodium storage capacity, wide availability, and enhanced safety.  However, their practical applications are still suffering from high vol. changes, poor electronic cond. and low utilization of active materials, resulting in unsatisfactory electrochem. performance.  In this study, a facile one-pot solvothermal method was developed to self-assemble and produce N-CoS2@C composites.  It was found from the expts. that the developed 3D polyhedral carbon-coated structure of N-CoS2@C can effectively reduce the diffusion lengths of sodium ions and electrons.  Carbon layer was also found firmly encapsulated the CoS2, where it can greatly release mech. stresses under high vol. change and also improve the electronic cond. of active materials.  The developed 3D polyhedral carbon-coated structure results in outstanding rate performance (738 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 reaching up to 86.2% theor. capacity and 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 A g-1) and extraordinary cycle stability (559 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles) when used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The research outcomes provide a novel design strategy for high-performance TMC electrodes and also a facile approach to fabricate promising anode materials for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrsk2SLlU9_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4dLyR5vYcCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhslCjt7jL&amp;md5=62651ec4430809b872230b1993494a1c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1126/science.1230444"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furukawa, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cordova, K.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The chemistry and applications of metal-organic frameworks</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Furukawa Hiroyasu; Cordova Kyle E; O'Keeffe Michael; Yaghi Omar M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (New York, N.Y.)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1230444</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Crystalline metal-organic frameworks (MOFs) are formed by reticular synthesis, which creates strong bonds between inorganic and organic units.  Careful selection of MOF constituents can yield crystals of ultrahigh porosity and high thermal and chemical stability.  These characteristics allow the interior of MOFs to be chemically altered for use in gas separation, gas storage, and catalysis, among other applications.  The precision commonly exercised in their chemical modification and the ability to expand their metrics without changing the underlying topology have not been achieved with other solids.  MOFs whose chemical composition and shape of building units can be multiply varied within a particular structure already exist and may lead to materials that offer a synergistic combination of properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQeDPOrmwnXDc-crCu0nI_sfW6udTcc2eba-K1aCujQ2bntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sbjs1yrsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=7eb2a10c62623ff8a27708ffe9561d45</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C4CS90059F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.-C. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kitagawa, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-Organic Frameworks (MOFs)</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-pot Synthesis of Metal-Organic Frameworks with Encapsulated Target Molecules and Their Applications for Controlled Drug Delivery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Haoquan; Zhang, Yuning; Liu, Leifeng; Wan, Wei; Guo, Peng; Nystroem, Andreas M.; Zou, Xiaodong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">962-968</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Many medical and chem. applications require target mols. to be delivered in a controlled manner at precise locations.  Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have high porosity, large surface area, and tunable functionality and are promising carriers for such purposes.  Current approaches for incorporating target mols. are based on multistep postfunctionalization.  Here, we report a novel approach that combines MOF synthesis and mol. encapsulation in a one-pot process.  We demonstrate that large drug and dye mols. can be encapsulated in zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF) crystals.  The mols. are homogeneously distributed within the crystals, and their loadings can be tuned.  We show that ZIF-8 crystals loaded with the anticancer drug doxorubicin (DOX) are efficient drug delivery vehicles in cancer therapy using pH-responsive release.  Their efficacy on breast cancer cell lines is higher than that of free DOX.  Our one-pot process opens new possibilities to construct multifunctional delivery systems for a wide range of applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqqgp1NMvi97Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxUUD9sXOcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVyrur7M&amp;md5=f875d3291a1478ab3387a18edda6f73d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acs.inorgchem.8b03316"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, S.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A ZnII-Based Metal-Organic Framework with a Rare tcj Topology as a Turn-On Fluorescent Sensor for Acetylacetone</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Shu-Li; Liu, Sui-Jun; Tian, Xue-Mei; Zheng, Teng-Fei; Cao, Chen; Niu, Chun-Yuan; Chen, Yong-Qiang; Chen, Jing-Lin; Huang, Haiping; Wen, He-Rui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A ZnII-based metal-org. framework (MOF) with a rare tcj topol. was solvothermally synthesized and displays relatively good thermal and chem. stabilities.  The complex is {[Zn3(bbib)2(ndc)3]·2DMF·2H2O}n (1), bbib = 1,3-bis(benzimidazolyl)benzene, H2ndc = 1,4-naphthalenedicarboxylic acid, and DMF = N,N-dimethylformamide.  The MOF can sensitively and selectively sense acetylacetone (acac) via a fluorescence enhancement effect with a detection limit of 0.10 ppm and good reusability, which demonstrates the first example of a MOF-based turn-on fluorescent sensor for acac.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3K8bLMsqcf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxUUD9sXOcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjvFGlur4%253D&amp;md5=09f80bb29928add2ba48ac89fdeee9c3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C8CE00837J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, S.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multivariant synthesis, crystal structures and properties of four nickel coordination polymers based on flexible ligands</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Sheng-Quan; Fang, Kang; Liu, Yong-Yao; Li, Ming-Xing; Liu, Sui-Jun; He, Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">CrystEngComm</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Four new Ni(II) coordination polymers, namely, [Ni(HL)(bpe)(H2O)2]n·nH2O (1), [Ni2(L)(bpe)(μ3-OH)(H2O)]n·3nH2O (2), [Ni(L)(bpe)(H2O)]n·[Ni0.5(bpe)0.5(H2O)2]n·nH2O (3) and [Ni(HL)(bpe)(H2O)]n·3nH2O (4) based on flexible ligands 5-(3-carboxybenzyloxy)-isophthalic acid (H3L) and 1,2-bis(4-pyridyl)ethane (bpe) have been successfully synthesized under different conditions.  Compds. 1 and 4 present two-dimensional sql layer structures, while compd. 2 exhibits a three-dimensional structure based on a tetranuclear Ni(II) cluster with (3,8)-connected tfz-d topol., and compd. 3 consists of a 2D sql anionic layer and 1D linear cationic chains, which are further entangled to give an interesting 2D + 1D → 3D poly-pseudorotaxane framework.  To det. the relationship between these diverse structures and external synthetic influence factors, we systematically change the molar ratios of the reactants, solvent and pH and study their effects.  Furthermore, the structural transformation from compd. 4 to 3 has also been investigated.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGriZtXVpbfxOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxUUD9sXOcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVSmt7%252FE&amp;md5=a6f5225ac5c9e8d56bd89b79c253c340</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201970371"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, W. Both complexes 1 and 2 present two-dimensional (3,8)-connected layer structures, and the point symbol is (3.42)2(34.46.56.68.73.8), but Fe2 in 2 is weakly coordinated to O5 as a trigonal bipyramidal geometry compared with the tetrahedral Co2 in 1, while complexes 3 and 4 exhibit three-dimensional "pillar-layer" structures with (3,8)-connected tfz-d net.  Nitrate anions with a rare μ2-η2 coordination mode take part in coordination, and rectangular channels along the c axis exist in 3 and 4.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two new mononuclear complexes, [Zn(3-Hcpa)2(H2O)4] (1) and [Zn(3,5,6-tcpa)2(H2O)4] [Zn(3,5,6-tcpa)2(H2O)2] (2) (3-H2cpa = 3-carboxy-phenoxyacetic acid, 3,5,6-Htcpa = 3,5,6-trichloro pyridine-2-oxyacetic acid), were synthesized and structurally characterized. Complex 2 is a co-crystal consisting of two discrete and stereochem. different complexes: one with an octahedrally, and the other a tetrahedrally coordinated zinc center.  The six-coordination about the first ZnII ion comprises four oxygen atoms from water (H2O) mols. and two from the carboxy groups of monodentate trans-related 3,5,6-tcpa- ligands.  The four-coordination about the second ZnII ion is comprised of two H2O ligands and two unidentate carboxy oxygen atoms from 3,5,6-tcpa- ligands.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian Blue Analogs for Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Baoqi; Han, Yu; Wang, Xiao; Bahlawane, Naoufal; Pan, Hongge; Yan, Mi; Jiang, Yinzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">iScience</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Non-lithium energy storage devices, esp. sodium ion batteries, are drawing attention due to insufficient and uneven distribution of lithium resources.  Prussian blue and its analogs (Prussian blue analogs [PBAs]), or hexacyanoferrates, are well-known since the 18th century and have been used for hydrogen storage, cancer therapy, biosensing, seawater desalination, and sewage treatment.  Owing to their unique features, PBAs are receiving increasing interest in the field of energy storage, such as their high theor. specific capacity, ease of synthesis, as well as low cost.  In this review, a general summary and evaluation of the applications of PBAs for rechargeable batteries are given.  After a brief review of the history of PBAs, their crystal structure, nomenclature, synthesis, and working principle in rechargeable batteries are discussed.  Then, previous works classified based on the combination of insertion cations and transition metals are analyzed comprehensively.  The review includes an outlook toward the further development of PBAs in electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3E8YXFnxObbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lje2jrbGtHB_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVajtbs%253D&amp;md5=8252f46be0d28c2dfc921e1ae9f9127e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405222"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance and Ultra-Stable Lithium-Ion Batteries Based on MOF-Derived ZnO@ZnO Quantum Dots/C Core-Shell Nanorod Arrays on a Carbon Cloth Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Guanhua; Hou, Sucheng; Zhang, Hang; Zeng, Wei; Yan, Feilong; Li, Cheng Chao; Duan, Huigao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

ZnO nanoarray-based electrode prepd. by growing ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell nanorod arrays (NRAs) on flexible carbon cloth (CC).  Applied as anode material, the as-synthesized ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell NRAs manifested high specific capacity and excellent cycling performance.  The self-supported ZnO@ZnO QDs/C NRAs exhibited a remarkable rate capability (a reversible capability of 1053, 913, 762, 591, and 530 mA-h g-1 at 100, 200, 400, 800, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.) and as well as remarkable cycling performance (approx. 11% capacity loss after 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1 with, a capacity retention of 699 mA-h g-1).                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multilayer CuO@NiO Hollow Spheres: Microwave-Assisted Metal-Organic-Framework Derivation and Highly Reversible Structure-Matched Stepwise Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Wenxiang; Sun, Weiwei; Wang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11462-11471</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A unique CuO@NiO microsphere with three-layer ball-in-ball hollow morphol. is successfully synthesized by Cu-Ni bimetallic org. frameworks.  The beforehand facile microwave-assisted prodn. of the Ni org. framework sphere is used as the template to induce the morphol. control of bimetallic oxides.  Designed by the controlled surface cationic exchange reactions between Cu and Ni ions, there is an elemental gradient (decreased amt. of CuO but increased amt. of NiO) from the shell to the core of the microsphere product.  This ternary metal oxide hollow structure is found to be very suitable for solving the crit. vol. expansion problem, which is crit. for all high-capacity metal oxide electrodes for lithium ion batteries.  A reversible larger-than-theor. capacity of 1061 mAh/gAPP can be retained after a repetitive 200 cycles without capacity fading compared to the initial cycle.  These excellent electrochem. properties are ascribed to the step-by-step lithium insertion reactions induced by the matched CuO@NiO compn. from the shell to the core and facilitated lithium/electron diffusion and accommodated vol. change in the porous bimetallic oxides microsphere with a multiple-layer yolk-shell nanostructure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpUoDhjlAxc5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lje2jrbGtHB_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Wru7fP&amp;md5=aaaf0b765f6f52712a2674996ccb46fd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.11.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic frameworks derived porous core/shellCoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced graphene oxide networks as anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xiaoli; Li, Zhaoqiang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel strategy is developed to synthesize metal-org. framework (MOF) derived core/shell structured CoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced grapheme oxide (RGO) on nickel foam (NF) as binder-free anode for high performance sodium-ion battery, through an in-situ low-temp. phosphidation process from ZIF-67 derived core/shell Co@C polyhedral structures.  The unique CoP@C-RGO-NF binder-free anode exhibits a remarkable electrochem. performance with outstanding cycling stability and high rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of 473.1 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  The excellent properties can be attributed to synergistic effects between core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons and RGO networks.  The unique core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons can offer more electrode/electrolyte contact area and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, while carbon layer shell can enhance electronic cond. and buffer vol. change, and prevent CoP from pulverization and aggregation.  Furthermore, 3D RGO networks can provide adequate surface areas for a high loading content of CoP and enhance charge transfer kinetics.  Meanwhile, RGO/NF can efficiently act as a binder and elec. conductor to interconnect the sep. CoP@C polyhedrons.  The present strategy for CoP@C-RGO-NF architectures can be extended to other novel electrodes for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEA0RBe_Ev_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lje2jrbGtHB_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGiurfO&amp;md5=95bf6b3529a8069bf6929d1f00eeaf34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA06916B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have been considered as promising precursors for the synthesis of 2D carbon materials for energy storage.  However, the high costs and low yields of the synthetic methods for 2D MOFs are major obstacles for the prepn. of 2D carbon materials from 2D MOFs.  Herein, a facile and low-cost bottom-up synthesis is reported of ultrathin Zn(bim)(OAc) MOF nanosheets (with a thickness of ∼5 nm and a high yield of ∼65%) and their derived N-doped porous ultrathin (2.5 ± 0.8 nm) carbon nanosheets (UT-CNSs) for energy storage.  The UT-CNSs exhibit a capacitance of 278 F g-1 at a high c.d. of 10 A g-1, which is the highest among the reported MOF-derived carbon materials for supercapacitor electrodes.  In addn., the UT-CNSs also exhibit a high reversible capacity of 553 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1 and retain 100% coulombic efficiency after 1000 cycles at 2 A g-1 as an anode material for lithium ion batteries.  The superior electrochem. properties of the UT-CNSs, esp. at high current densities, are mainly due to their ultrathin morphol., large sp. surface area, high cond., and suitable porous structure.  This work provides a new strategy for the high-yield and low-cost synthesis of ultrathin MOF nanosheets as well as 2D carbon materials and their metal or metal oxide composites for various applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpIx7k273K_X7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljL8BLcnH7LUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtV2qsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=83743175bd84a167cb35424cb7a9124d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA05554H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-organic frameworks derived hollow NiS<sub>2</sub> spheres encased in graphene layers for enhanced sodium-ion storage</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14077</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14082</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic frameworks derived hollow NiS2 spheres encased in graphene layers for enhanced sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bi, Ran; Zeng, Cheng; Huang, Huawen; Wang, Xinping; Zhang, Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14077-14082</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel disulfide (NiS2) is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Due to the vol. expansion issue and intrinsic low cond., conventional NiS2-based anodes exhibit unsatisfactory Na+ storage performance far below their high theor. specific capacity.  Here, hollow NiS2 microspheres assembled from small NiS2 nanoparticles embedded in graphene layers (hollow NiS2@G) were successfully prepd. by one-step annealing of Ni-MOFs involving simultaneous carbonization and sulfidation.  Benefitting from the hollow and porous structure, highly graphitized carbon protective layers and large mass loading of NiS2, the as-prepd. hollow NiS2@G is developed as a high-performance anode for SIBs, and delivers an increased capacity of 848 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles and an excellent rate capability of 527.8 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1.  The comprehensive material characterization and electrochem. investigations demonstrate the one-step calcination as a simple and effective strategy in fabricating MOFs-derived nanocomposites for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrknD-jgRCjz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljL8BLcnH7LUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1Cis7rK&amp;md5=2f11c25f9801b5960f76138339d24ca4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA10448K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-rich carbon coated CoSnO3 derived from in situ construction of a Co-MOF with enhanced sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhao, Ganggang; Ge, Peng; Yin, Dulin; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4839-4847</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, N-rich carbon coated interconnected CoSnO3 nanoboxes (CoSnO3-NCs) with controllable amts. of N-rich carbon ranging from 7.5% to 24.6% were firstly prepd. by the carbonization of CoSnO3-MOFs.  Impressively, the prepn. of CoSnO3-MOFs has been realized for the first time by directly utilizing CoSnO3 as the precursor under solvent-free conditions, bridging between the cobalt(II) ion in the skeleton of CoSnO3 and the 2-methylimidazole.  Interestingly, the growth of these CoSnO3-MOFs can be manipulated by changing the amt. of 2-methylimidazole used, resulting in a tunable N-rich carbon content.  Furthermore, the electrochem. storage behavior of these materials for SIBs was initially explored.  Compared with the pure CoSnO3, the as-resulted CoSnO3-NC materials showed largely enhanced sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of 493.9 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles.  Moreover, the as-prepd. materials showed an excellent high rate storage performance with a remarkable capacity of 273.8 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  This work provides a new approach for constructing Co-MOFs as well as providing an efficient N-rich carbon-coating route, which may be expanded to other Co-based oxides and can greatly expand the development of new species of Co-based MOFs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4Sm6TP9CmybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljL8BLcnH7LUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXivFGiu7k%253D&amp;md5=da727123d227559645f0c4cce08cfc81</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705146"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Indra, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paik, U.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal Organic Framework Derived Materials: Progress and Prospects for the Energy Conversion and Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible lithiation-delithiation chemistry in cobalt based metal organic framework nanowire electrode engineering for advanced lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Huawei; Shen, Lisha; Wang, Jing; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15411-15419</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a challenging issue, minimizing metal org. framework (MOF) bulks to nanoscale is of great significance in deepening their application for energy storage, catalysis, sensing, etc.  MOF nanostructures, particularly nanowires, are highly desirable because of their fast transport kinetics, good flexibility, and universal structural compatibility.  Taking a polycarboxylate based cobalt coordination polymer (CoCOP) as an example, we presented one-dimensional (1D) MOF nanowires by a facile and scalable method.  The CoCOP nanowires deliver an impressive lithium ion storage capacity of more than 1100 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1.  Besides the high energy and power performance (875 W h kg-1 and 6422 W kg-1) comparable to that of recently advanced metal oxide hybrid electrodes, they also exhibit excellent long term cycling stability for more than 1000 cycles for fully reversible lithiation-delithiation chem. based on a joint mechanism of intercalation-like structural deformation and Co2+/Co conversion reactions.  Typical full cells with CoCOP nanowire anodes and com. LiFePO4 powder cathodes (CoCOP-LiFePO4) also demonstrate excellent cyclability and fast charge-discharge capability with a capacity retention of 83% for more than 300 cycles at a 1C rate (1C corresponds to a one hour discharge process).  Besides, a large capacity of 138 mA h g-1 at 0.1C and a high specific energy of 222 W h kg-1 (based on the total wt. of CoCOP and LiFePO4) also substantiate their superior performance to common com. energy storage and conversion devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpia0Awh9Z1cbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljL8BLcnH7LUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVKisrzE&amp;md5=88aa2b5e08f8fafda19d9614caa38d45</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.03.052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural and chemical synergistic effect of CoS nanoparticles and porous carbon nanorods for high-performance sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Limin; Zhang, Kai; Sheng, Jinzhi; An, Qinyou; Tao, Zhanliang; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering inherent large structural deterioration of conversion-type anode materials during repeated sodiation/desodiation process, the ingenious integration of both nanostructure engineering and chem. hybridization is highly desirable and challenging.  Here, ultrafine CoS nanoparticles embedded in porous carbon nanorods (denoted as 7-CoS/C) were facilely fabricated via simultaneous in-situ carbonization and sulfidation of Co-metal org. frameworks (Co-MOF) and have been applied as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Benefiting from the advantageous embedding architecture between the nanoparticles and porous nanorods, the 7-CoS/C delivers long-term cycling stability (542 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles with a capacity retention of 91.4% at 1 A g-1) and excellent rate performance (discharge capacities of 510 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 and 356 mAh g-1 even at 40 A g-1), which is proved to be characterized of partial pseudocapacitive behaviors during the sodiation/desodiation process.  In addn., Na3V2(PO4)3/7-CoS/C full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 has been assembled and exhibits a capacity of 352 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1.  This meaningful approach can be extended to build embedded porous structure of other hybrid composites for next-generation energy-storage technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9KtRozkoFx7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljL8BLcnH7LUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlslejtbs%253D&amp;md5=6f81f0741eecaa1345bac17a099cb17f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b11984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Morphology CoS2 Anchored on N-Doped Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Gong, Lunlun; Shi, Long; Zhou, Ting; Deng, Yurui; Zhang, Heping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">31441-31451</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (NIBs) have attracted increasing attention given the fact that sodium is relatively more plentiful and affordable than lithium for sustainable and large-scale energy storage systems.  However, the shortage of electrode materials with outstanding comprehensive properties has limited the practical implementations of NIBs.  Among all the discovered anode materials, transition-metal sulfide has been proven as one of the most competitive and promising ones due to its excellent redox reversibility and relatively high theor. capacity.  In this study, double-morphol. N-doped CoS2/multichannel carbon nanofibers composites (CoS2/MCNFs) are precisely designed, which overcome common issues such as the poor cycling life and inferior rate performance of CoS2 electrodes.  The conductive 3D interconnected multichannel nanostructure of CoS2/MCNFs provides efficient buffer zones for the release of mech. stresses from Na+ ions intercalation/deintercalation.  The synergy of the diverse structural features enables a robust frame and a rapid electrochem. reaction in CoS2/MCNFs anode, resulting in an impressive long-term cycling life of 900 cycles with a capacity of 620 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 (86.4% theor. capacity) and a surprisingly high-power output.  The proposed design in this study provides a rational and novel thought for fabricating electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIewUzTT2U7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhr8Q959l8feg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhs1WitLnF&amp;md5=d5a670e5d0bfd28f24c4512e95fa9d03</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201803690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.                 10.1002/adma.201503015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6702-6707%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BF.%2BJiao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DTin%2BNanodots%2BEncapsulated%2Bin%2BPorous%2BNitrogen-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2Ba%2BFree-Standing%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201503015&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b22169&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201503015&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6702-6707</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small Sn nanodots (1-2 nm) were delicately encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers through electrospinning and thermal treatment.  The size and content of Sn particles can be controlled by changing reaction conditions.  When evaluated as binder- and current collector-free anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries, Sn NDs@PNC nanofibers delivered a reversible capacity of 633 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, a capacity of 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 000 mA g-1 and 483 mA h g-1 over 1300 cycles at 2000 mA g-1 were achieved.  To our knowledge, this is the highest rate performance and cyclic stability of tin for Na storage.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of Sn NDs@PNC is attributed to the following: First, the ultra-small Sn NDs (1-2 nm) decreases the abs. strain and improve the utilization rate of active materials during sodiation/de-sodiation process; second, the uniform distribution of Sn NDs in the fibrous carbon matrix is an important factor to generate a balanced stress over the whole composite with maintaining the integrity of the electrode upon prolonged cycling; third, the 1D porous N-doped carbon frame can interlink into a 3D conductive network, which facilitates the electron and Na+ diffusion kinetics and buffers the large vol. fluctuation of Sn NDs and prevents their pulverization and aggregation.  Carbon fibers also serve as both current collector and conductive material - this avoids the common loss of electrochem. contact between the active materials and the current collector/conductive additives, and reduces the inactive wt. and vol. of cells thus improving the energy d.  This simple and scalable synthesis as well as the promising electrochem. performance encourages application of Sn-based materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnXAQ9MCRr0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhr8Q959l8feg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks77J&amp;md5=c6f2a6fad6ab6e844a9149e974f0edf1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/jp508698q"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, S.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Morphological Effect of Graphene Nanosheets on Ultrathin CoS Nanosheets and Their Applications for High-Performance Li-Ion Batteries and Photocatalysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Shaofeng; Jin, Zhitong; Liu, Hong; Wang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">118</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">25355-25364</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A unique CoS-graphene sheet-on-sheet nanocomposite has been successfully prepd. by anchoring CoS nanosheets on the surface of graphene nanosheets (GNS) with the assistance of the structure-directing agent of ethylenediamine.  The shape and size of the introduced CoS nanosheets can be further adjusted by varying the amt. of GNS.  The unprecedented sheet-like CoS structure is believed to be matched well with GNS basically due to their similar two-dimensional structure with max. contact areas between two components.  The strong interaction between CoS and the underlying highly conductive graphene can facilitate fast electron and ion transport and improve structure stability of the composite.  The composite with 26.2% GNS displays excellent electrochem. performance when evaluated as an anode for rechargeable lithium-ion battery.  A larger-than-theor. reversible capacity of 898 mAh/g can be delivered after 80 cycles at 0.1 C along with excellent high-rate cycling performance. Characterization by using X-ray diffraction (XRD), SEM (SEM), and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) confirmed the successful incorporation of the cobalt (Co) dopant into the wurtzite ZnO structure, which led to a decreased particle size for the doped compd.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manganese silicate hollow spheres enclosed in reduced graphene oxide as anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Yanjiao; Ulissi, Ulderico; Bresser, Dominic; Ma, Yuan; Ji, Yuanchun; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein is presented a new composite material consisting of nanostructured Mn silicate hollow spheres enclosed in a matrix of reduced graphene oxide (rGO), synthesized via a facile and low-cost hydrothermal method.  The hollow structure provides free space to accommodate the vol. expansion occurring upon lithiation, while the rGO facilitates the electron transport, thus enhancing the lithiation kinetics.  Remarkably, the composite provides a continuously increasing reversible capacity up to ∼1300 mAh g-1 after 350 cycles.  This increase in capacity is ascribed in part to the steadily rising fraction of Mn2+/Mn3+ being oxidized to Mn4+ as well as the reversible formation of the solid electrolyte interphase.  The particle morphol., in fact, remains unaltered, as evidenced by ex situ SEM - even after 350 cycles.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4GczM5ztnng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/nl504764m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muller, G.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-layer and few-layer transition metal dichalcogenides have been extensively studied for their electronic properties, but their energy-storage potential has not been well explored.  This paper describes the structural and electrochem. properties of few-layer TiS2 nanocrystals.  The two-dimensional morphol. leads to very different behavior, compared to corresponding bulk materials.  Only small structural changes occur during lithiation/delithiation and charge storage characteristics are consistent with intercalation pseudocapacitance, leading to materials that exhibit both high energy and power d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrMEHWzqPoFmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4GczM5ztnng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXit12msLg%253D&amp;md5=8a06a4dfc4a4da03e4c3cc5852b9c947</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b05566"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Na-Ion Storage Boosts High Rate and Areal Capacity of Self-Branched 2D Layered Metal Chalcogenide Nanoarrays</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Liang, Pei; Chen, Zhen; Bai, Linyi; Shen, He; Liu, Xiaoxu; Xia, Xinhui; Zhao, Yanli; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundant reserve and low cost of sodium have provoked tremendous evolution of Na-ion batteries (SIBs) in the past few years, but their performances are still limited by either the specific capacity or rate capability.  Attempts to pursue high rate ability with maintained high capacity in a single electrode remains even more challenging.  Here, an elaborate self-branched 2-dimensional SnS2 (B-SnS2) nanoarray electrode is designed by a facile hot bath method for Na storage.  This interesting electrode exhibits areal reversible capacity of ∼3.7 mAh/cm2 (900 mAh/g) and rate capability of 1.6 mAh/cm2 (400 mAh/g) at 40 mA/cm2 (10 A/g).  Improved extrinsic pseudocapacitive contribution is demonstrated as the origin of fast kinetics of an alloying-based SnS2 electrode.  Sodiation dynamics anal. based on 1st-principles calcns., ex-situ HRTEM, in situ impedance, and in situ Raman technologies verify the S-edge effect on the fast Na+ migration and reversible and sensitive structure evolution during high-rate charge/discharge.  The excellent alloying-based pseudocapacitance and unsatd. edge effect enabled by self-branched surface nanoengineering could be a promising strategy for promoting development of SIBs with both high capacity and high rate response.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr0qsYefl4nTbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4GczM5ztnng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslCgsb3O&amp;md5=90f5040a1baba0248c7f7165e1b8fe4f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/C5CC02564H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shadike, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, M.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li4zXe3A3FJPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE03367A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li4zXe3A3FJPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2mtbnN&amp;md5=be5958dc01f38deeacf6a2a0eb32101f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.
